<Content>Amazing Experience! We had originally booked our trip through Expedia, which we encountered several problems with in the time before our visit. I have to stress the friendly in pet-friendly. There are chain hotels that do allow pets, but the staff at the Nine Zero truly cater to you and your pet! Our dog was personally greeted (as were we) by all the staff including the doorman, reception agents, and more. There was room service, which our dog loved! They brought him an amazing dinner and dessert on a platter, he could barely contain his excitement when it arrived!The Nine Zero gets it right, down to the smallest detail, and they were helpful before, during, and after our trip. If you are looking for an amazing experience from a world-class staff, this is the place to be!

<Author>SkyeTraveler
<Content>Central location, nice view We paid extra for one of the premier view king rooms and thought the price was well worth it. From our room we could look down onto the Granary Burying Ground, and northeast towards Cambridge. Nice to be able to look over the rooftops; much better than looking straight onto another building.The bed was super comfortable. I would have liked a bathtub, but the shower was fine. Lovely L'Occitane soaps, too.We were able to walk to the waterfront, the North End, Beacon Hill and Back Bay. The Park St. T station is located very close by if you're not a keen walker. If you want to take the T from the Airport, the Blue Line will take you straight to Government Center, and it's about a 5-10 minute walk from there. Or change to the Green Line and get off at Park Street.Originally, we thought of booking the Mandarin Oriental, but Nine Zero was literally half the price. It's good value, and we'll probably be back.

<Content>The most atrocious experience I had Cons: - Reading great things about this hotel, I booked it and I was terribly dissappointed at how it turned out to be. - Deluxe and premier rooms have no view at all. They will either have a window in front of you or a concrete wall.- The tables, desk and phone were dusty, and not cleaned in advance.- The bathroom floor got all wet and called customer service to come in as quickly as possible, told them myself. Receptionist called me 2 hours later to tell me that they did not knock on my door because I had the private sign. Take into account that a first customer service came in the room to see the problem and suggested to call someone else to solve it. Of course he did knock in the door regardless of the sign.- The TV had terrible reception and noise every 5 seconds. - There is no complimentary drinks or food in the minibar. Everything has to be paid at checkout, even a cookie is 5 dollars. - To request some bathroom appliances they charge you more than 6 dollars per request. - Parking is 38 dollars, not including taxes, per night. And they don't tell you where the car is parked or let you go see the car. Parking fees are not specified when booking accomodations in this hotel. - The location of the hotel is not at all good or convenient. I read more than 50 reviews relating to the location of the hotel being so good, and found out that it wasn't at all. Everything is far away. - The hotel charges for its business center. - Your booking doesn't include complimentary breakfast, taking into account that it charges no less than 200 dollars a night. - The design is terrible, there are long tall curtains everywhere that cover what it's supposed to be a nice wall design, or maybe a picture.- The breakfast menu will not cost less than 20 dollars for one person and that doesn't include what is usually requested.- The less expensive dinner menu will be the same for twice what a regular dinner will cost you at a regular restaurant like Chilys or Bertuccis. - They charge 10 dollars for a map. A map which is free about 10 blocks from the hotel in a city hall area. - The only thing a got from this place is how they want to squeeze more dollars. The taxed 80 cents for a coca cola I drank one night. Also, the first thing they ask is when will your dinner reservations be, of course, the cheapest dinner plate will run you over 40 dollars per person!.- I upgraded my room and at 7 or 8 am heard a lot of noise on the 12th floor. - There is only 1 bathrobe for use. The rest, even socks, are IN the room, but for sale only.Terrible hotel, I've stayed over 100 hotels in different countries and the US, this has been the worse. But why the worse? basically because you pay as a luxury hotel and expect the best. Hotwire ranks this place as a 4.5 star hotel. I certainly will give it a 3 like Ramada or Holiday Inn. My upfront suggestion to a couple, young people and everybody that has a sense of reality, do not spend time or money in the Nine Zero Hotel in Boston. Give your money to charity and you will feel much better. That's what I did after I came home.

<Content>Cool Hotel, Warm Welcome I zeroed in on this hotel for a special occasion and was very satisfied with my choice. The location is ideal for walking to many of Boston's features and it's very near the Park Street T stop, which has access to red and green lines, so getting to further points is simple. Don't laugh--clean towels---meaning in spite of the hotel having a green initiative that asks guests to hang up and reuse towels, ours were replaced daily. <Author>tymelyron
<Content>9.0 for Nine Zero Stayed at Nine Zero last weekend in a Queen Queen Premier room; we had gotten a great promotional rate after having signed up on the Kimpton website. There are only 10 rooms on each floor and spaced well so it was very quiet and private. The room was very clean, as was the bathroom, and the decor was ultra modern. The bed had multiple pillows of differing firmness, with more varieties to be had at the desk. The bed was most comfortable with a soft pillow top. The staff was most courteous, and the location was great, within a 10 minute walking distance to the TD Banknorth Center and the North End. My only issues were no free access to a computer for email (charges apply in the business center) and no complimentary coffee available in the morning (though a coffee machine for the room can be requested.) Other than that, I would highly recommend Nine Zero.

<Author>CruzanTom
<Content>Nine Zero - Pros and Cons I have stayed in many Boston Hotels and recently stayed at the Nine Zero twice. Pros: Centrally located, Excellent and courteous Staff (I had good experiences with all, including front desk, valets, housekeeping and room service), good restaurant and bar in hotel, free wine hour each evening, free WiFi, comfortable beds.Cons: Rooms are a bit small and high priced (but much in mid-town Boston is, too), furniture is old, TVs are old with poor speakers and color adjustment (in both recent stays my TV speaker was cracked causing a lisp sound), the robes and lingerie provided in the closet seemed strange (leopard or cheetah patterned boxers and camisoles).Suggestion to Management - Upgrade the rooms. Do what it takes to keep your staff happy, they are wonderful.

<Author>skigator93
<Content>Outstanding Place to Stay in Boston We just spent 4 glorious nights at the Nine Zero for our 10th Anniversary. The desk staff and concierge are all warm and friendly and the complimentary nightly wine tasting is a nice touch. The housekeeping staff was superb, both in cleaning the room in the morning and providing nightly turn-down service.The rooms are nice sized for Boston and the hotel has paid a lot of attention to detail. The king bed was very comfortable and covered with gazillion thread count sheets. The pillows started out fluffy, but then flatten out when you lay your head on them - no big deal though. The bathroom was roomy and water pressure was excellent. The toiletries were smelled great and were in adequate supply. The mini bar was well-stocked with more choices than the average hotel, including a martini bar with shaker, rimmers and several flavorings.The location is outstanding - virtually right across the street from Granary Burial Ground and Boston Commons, and a short walk (less than 10 minutes) to Fanueil Hall, Quincy Market, North End, etc. The Bean Town Pub next door was a very cozy pub and perfect for a bowl of chowder and a pint. The only negatives? Room service is a little slow - we requested a couple forks to eat our take out pastries from the North End. After about 15 minutes, we gave up and cancelled the request. Also, the hotel is a little too focused on selling you items from the room. Most hotels offer the robes for sale - but this one had pajamas hanging in the closet for sale, full-sized bottles of the toiletries, CDs, etc. etc. It was a little annoying, but really, who cares if that is the only negative thing to say about a hotel?!?I would highly recommend the Nine Zero for your next stay in Boston!

<Author>TravelFan_01
<Content>Loved it!! We stayed at Nine Zero for 3 nights, as an early 30th birthday present for my husband. It was on a whim that I thought of Boston so I rang up my travel agent to see if she had any weekend deals. I hadn't had time to do my research as I always usually do before I book a hotel but she knew the kind of hotels that we liked. She found a great deal for Nine Zero and told us that we would love it, so I trusted her judgement and went for it. We couldn't be more delighted that we did.When we arrived at Nine Zero, it was pretty late (about 10pm) because we had a nightmare with our flights and had been delayed in Philadelphia for a number of hours. So we were looking rather exhausted and bedraggled when we entered the beautiful lobby to say the least! So it was really nice to be greeted with a warm smile at the front desk when we checked in and we were immediately much more relaxed and at ease. We were given the keys to our room and we made our way up there through the gorgeously decorated public areas. It all felt so warm and welcoming and I'm sure that they have some kind of scent pumping through the heating or air con vents because the hotel even smelt beautiful!When we got to our room, we were absolutely delighted with it. It was spacious, clean and was decorated beautifully. The bathroom was lovely and the shower was great with really good pressure. The tolietries were gorgeous too. We found the bed really comfortable and everything that we could have wanted was in the room. We felt completely at home. The view out of the window was really pretty too.Because we had arrived at the hotel so late, we didn't really want to venture out to look for somewhere to eat so we decided to order room service on our first night. I rang up and ordered our meals and was told that it would be about 15 minutes. Over half an hour later, it still hadn't arrived so I rang up to check where it was. I wouldn't normally do that but we were so tired, having been on the go for almost 24 hours with no sleep and no opportunity to eat since the flight to Philadelphia. All we really wanted to do have dinner quickly and go straight to sleep. We were told that there had been a rush on in the restuarant but that it would arrive at any minute, and I almost felt a bit guilty for ringing up! Sure enough, it arrived soon afterwards and the lady who brought the food couldn't apologise enough. She even asked if there was anything we'd like to make up for the inconvenience which was very kind, although we didn't take her up on the offer. We just ordered cheeseburgers and fries and I have to say, that it really was tasty. It was fresh and hot, although the portion size was too much for us! My husband and I never happened to be in the hotel during the wine hour but it is a lovely little extra and a nice way for guests to socialise.The location of the hotel was absolutely superb. It was about a 10 minute walk to Quincy Market, 5 minutes to Downtown Crossing and probably less than 5 minutes to Boston Common. There were plenty of shops, restaurants and a cinema around the immediate area as well the more historical sights and walks of Boston just steps away. The general ambience of the hotel was just lovely. It was such a welcoming place to come back to after a day's sightseeing and I can't really can't fault the place.If we ever return to Boston in the future, we won't even think of looking at any other hotel but Nine Zero.

<Author>Raerton
<Content>The Good, the Bad, the Ugly Visited Boston with my father the weekend of Aug 15-17, each staying in our own Queen Premier View room.The Good: unbeatable location in Boston, easy walking distance to many attractions, Boston Common, the waterfront, the subway, trolley tour stops etc. Rooms were well appointed and clean, the bed was extremely comfortable, liked the kooky robes in the room. Front desk extremely polite (although at times nauseatingly so).The Bad: housekeeping staff on multiple occasions entered the room as they knocked on the door, giving no reaction time to even say Just a second or even make one's self decent. Housekeeping did not replace wet towels left on the floor in the bathroom, or even hang them up. No water glasses in the bathroom, my father (who is half blind) had to hunt for glasses in the room, which are hidden BEHIND the mixers at the back of the mini-bar. The stopper in the tub in my father's room was stuck down, preventing water from draining out (he had to take apart the mechanism to allow drainage). Finally, the Premier View of his room on the 14th floor was of multiple air conditioning units on an adjacent rooftop.The Ugly: I was in room 1903, which is adjacent to the Cloud Nine Suite. I did not know the nature of that suite at the time, but by 2:30am Saturday morning I honestly thought it was a dance club. The loud music, people partying in the halls and drunken arguments were endless. There was a constant stream of partiers going in and out of that room. Two calls to the front desk yielded no results and it wasn't until a third (in which I offered to call the police myself) that front desk staff and security showed up on the scene to throw them out. Obviously, there was no rest that night for myself.I appreciate that the Cloud Nine Suite is likely a big moneymaker for the hotel and a selling point for the hotel. It is my opinion that certainly the adjoining rooms should not be rented when the Cloud Nine Suite is occupied, as I doubt this is the first or last time noise has been an issue on the 19th floor.Having said this, the front desk at checkout was very accommodating (in the only way that matters, as apologies are quite useless in my opinion) but this still created unnecessary anxiety.Overall I think the Nine Zero has a lot going for it, but there are many small details that need to be addressed by management.

<Author>sammybaka
<Content>Awesome hotel Ninezero is one of the best hotel experiences I've had in recent memory. It's got a fantastic location near Boston Common and Downtown Crossing, with easy access to both the green line (e.g: back bay) and blue line (e.g: airport). The hotel is tastefully decorated, and everywhere from the lobby, elevator, room and bathroom were well lit and arranged. It even smelled nice and fresh.The staff was excellent and friendly, eager to help and provided very useful information. They all seemed to carry a genuine smile and happy to do their job. For example, I asked where to find the boston Duck Tour (highly recommended btw), and I was immediately informed of the two closest locations around the hotel, but she referred me to the concierge desk to book the tour in advance just in case. The gentleman at the concierge was equally friendly, and offered concise directions on where to locate the duck tour at the Prudential center. Furthermore, we were fortunate to find out in advance that the Saturday tour was already fully booked, and we quickly snatched a preferred time on the next day. All of this was done by the Hotel concierge desk without extra charge. In addition, he recommended that at the end of the Freedom Trail we could ride a ferry from Charlestown back to Long Wharf. That's valuable information I didn't have, and was glad to save a bunch of walking time.I just have two minor criticisms: (1) could use a little more towel hanging space in the bathroom, and (2) the air conditioner was very cold, and the room remained pretty cold even after I turned it off, but it's manageable.I will definitely return to this hotel in the future. Great location, great room and great service all at a good price. Highly recommended.

<Author>S_G.UK
<Content>Great hotel, great location, good value in an expensive city This is a lovely hotel. Hotels in Boston are pricey so I thought that this place was good value - expensive but good standard, really nice contemporary decor. Stayed here with my mother for a long weekend in March and thoroughly enjoyed our experience. It's excellently placed for sight seeing in Boston, which is frankly a small and accessible/easily navigable city. We never ate in the restaurant but it seemed very much 'the' place for out of towners 'in the know' and locals alike. We chilled in the bar, where the bar staff were cool and reserved, but polite and quite sweet - letting my mum and I taste the cockails before we decided what to have next!This hotel has two main drawbacks; firstly, the heinously expensive mini bar - easily addressed by staying out or frequenting the 7 Eleven down the street! the second issue is slightly harder to resolve - our room looked out over a side street which obviously housed the bottle banks and trash bins for nearby bars, or perhaps the hotel's own. Whatever - the noise of rubbish and glass being thrown into the bins, and then the early morning street cleaners was pretty disturbing. The hotel should invest in some better soundproofing for these rooms - this is not a bargain basement hostel - at these prices and with the level of comfort and style offered in the rooms, this really tainted the otherwise great experience. Oh, and the concierge could have been more helpful. We were trying to find and book some restaurants recommended by a friend and he made no offer to call and book on our behalf, etc. Would have been a nice touch.

<Author>JCLON
<Content>Rien a redire Stayed at the NineZero because they had a great deal on Expedia. I have stayed at Kimpton Hotels before and never really enjoyed it. The decor is usually flamboyant and has a cheap feel to itself. Here, the style is very toned down. I stayed here on business but it is a great leisure hotel as well. There is a cemetery across the street where Samuel Adams a buried. On a less morbid note, you'll enjoy Park Street T station with the red and green lines, proximity to Faneuil Hall, Public Garden and Copley place which you can walk to in about 15 to 20 minutes. The staff is very sweet. Always very polite, obviously very well trained. Smiles abound. The one thing that really prompted the 5 out of 5 rating was the room service food. As much as I was not particularly impressed with the breakfast, I absolutely loved the room service dinner food. I asked for a fruit salad which was not on the menu but that was not a problem. A superb salad of very fresh fruit was delivered within 15 minutes. A true delight. I also had the best French Fries in a very long time. Oh, and when I asked for a rare steak, guess what, it was delivered rare! All in all, I highly recommend this hotel. Do not expect a 5 start, this is only a 4* but a 4* with no glitch, a rare occurance in the hotel world.

<Author>cubalibre3
<Content>Good Location -- Nice Boutique Hotel This was great hotel, centrally located. My husband and I stayed for a weekend. We booked our hotel through AMEX using our points, so it was a steal. After reading the reviews I was a bit nervous, but compared to the other boutiques, 9-0 had the least amount of bad reviews. We arrived late on Friday and the staff were very nice and welcoming, especially Brian from the valet service. I had called ahead and asked for a room on the highest floor and they said they put a note on my file. When we arrived to our room, which we paid extra for a view, I was disappointed that our view was of a building across the way. We were then moved to a room on their top floor and the view was better, but honestly, I would not pay the additional money for the view, unless you want to look at the top of buildings. The beds were comfy, the shower was good and I liked knowing I was staying at an eco-friendly hotel.We didn't have any noise complaints, except that the suite next door let their alam clock ring for an hour, but when we called guest services they sent someone up to take care of it immediately. Overall it was a great stay -- if you like the swank, boutique hotels. I found the people of Boston to be a little less than warm and fuzzy, but the staff including Scotty, the concierge were more than happy to accommodate! You won't be disappointed.

<Author>Greg187
<Content>Still Great! Just stayed at the Nine-Zero and am happy to report that it is still a great destination when visiting Boston. I haven't been there since the first year they opened and was delighted to see that most things are still up to par. The most alluring feature of this hotel is the location - I can't imagine a more convenient hotel in all of Boston. It's sleek/hip design is also very cool. But, like all trendy hotels, it seems to tire from hipness. While still sharp, nothing really has changed since I've been there 4 or so years ago.The room is very comfortable and stylish but was showing slight signs of wear (minor wall scuffs, slightly aging furniture). Also, on my first visit the robes and towels were Frette and that was no longer the case. The Mario Russo products were great but seemed to be smaller in size. And the cheap plastic made it difficult to actually get the shampoo or conditioner out. And, as mentioned in another review...it is a little tacky that there are so many things for sale in the room. The bed was super comfortable and very roomy. A luggage rack would have been nice.One great addition from my last stay was the evening cocktail hour. Nice wines were served in the lobby from 5-6. A nice touch. Staff was friendly and helpful. Needed some extra soap and it was sent up promptly. As instructed, when I needed my car I called about a half hour before hand. I came downstairs and it was ready and waiting. Although the $38 fee is quite steep!The Nine-Zero is no bargain but look around the web. I got a great rate through one of their promotions and it was actually a little cheaper than comparable hotels such as the Hilton.

<Author>thelbie
<Content>I'm Hooked!! We travel once a year to Boston to attend a Red Sox game and usually make it an overnight to enjoy a dinner in the North End (such great Italian food) then a leisurely stroll around town. This year we decided to stay at the Nine Zero as we also had a great deal on travzoo. We had heard about this hotel from Conde Nast's great ratings. We cannot say enough about this Hotel. From the get go service was magnificent. We were checked in promptly and what I think is a good gesture is the staff comes from behind the desk to give you your keys making it more personal. We were given an upgrade to the 19th floor overlooking the Skyline of Boston from one floor to ceiling window and the City Govt Center from the other. The room was smaller than I expected but other than that no complaints from us. Very clean, large shower, very comfy beds on which you can have any type of pillows you want just by asking. We didn't use the minibar (never do) and didn't watch TV but did make use of the music. From 5-6 there is a wine reception in the lobby which we did partake before going out to dinner. A very nice touch. The staff goes out of their way to welcome you and make you feel very comfortable. Kudos to Shavangi who was just great. We checked out but left our bag there and when we returned she welcomed us with a smile and a genuine hello and offered us some wine. I thought because we had checked out already that we weren't eligible for lack of a better word. But she said we were still guests. We are now hooked on this hotel and will be staying on our next trip to Boston. Nine Zero should be very proud of their staff, the best I have seen yet.

<Content>Unimpressive We were in Boston for a conference and our first hotel had no rooms for Saturday night so we booked elsewhere only to find the other hotel had overbooked. We called my credit card travel agency and they found us the room at Nine Zero. The city was packed, so we were happy to get a room, but were not impressed at all. The staff was very young and peppy but most were not very helpful. I don't think it was an attitude issue but rather a lack of experience. However, the Concierge was very knowledgeable and helped us pick an excellent Italian restaurant in the North End for dinner. She went out of her way to map out the walking route and to call and confirm that reservations were still available. She also followed up with us when we returned. Other staff members did not seem to know their way around the hotel itself and were not versed in helping out-of-towners. The room was clean with newer furnishings. It was mod and chic but with a corporate office feel. The most annoying, yet funny, detail was the price tags. It seemed like everything in the room was for sale! Like this robe? It can be yours! Enjoyed the bath products? Here is a package of regular sized products that you can buy? Need aspirin? You can buy it here! While some might find it cool or convenient to buy up the hotel room for the same feel at home, we found it annoying.

<Author>WMadge
<Content>Wonderful Hotel and a great location The Hotel is great, a perfect location centrally located for all areas and attractions. I can see why the other reviews were so complementary, this is the 4th Kimpton Hotel we have stayed in and it was just as good as the others have been.The Hotel is well managed and the staff represent this well. I asked to see the top floor room Cloud 9 which they were happy to do. The staff member who took me up there was extremely helpful and informative and very keen to tell me what a great Hotel this was to work for. This atmosphere comes across.We asked for a high room and were pleased to be on the 17th floor with a great view State House, it was a very quiet room.We had breakfast once, I can highly recommend the pancakes we ate out other times. We tried The Paramount in Charles street, Down the hill (Beacon Street) and on the right. get there early and enjoy the atmosphere, it is not a place for lingering but worth going to. Charles Street has some wonderful older shops to browse in once you have had breakfast. There are a lot of coffee shops around the Hotel but not so many breakfast places, if you want more than bagels and muffins. Not many diners, there is one down the hill at South Street though.Restaurants we enjoyed and were recommended to us by a Bostonian friend were Mooo just around the corner in beacon Street from the Hotel, not cheap but good quality and atmosphere. The hotel bar on the 2nd floor was great, plus the bar food.The Beantown Pub next door is a great place to watch sport and have a beer and bar food and a game of pool. Plus not far to get back to the Hotel!The Daily Catch is a small restaurant that you would pass by without a thought in Hanover Street North End. I was told to go there and did so for a late lunch...wonderful. A handed down family run restaurant with seafood that melts in your mouth. In the evening people queue aroudn the block so my recommendation would be a late lunch after whale watching if you take the 10.30 boat. You have to pay in cash though so beware!Whale watching was fantastic if you want to get out of the City for a few hours. The Boston Harbour Cruise catamaran was fast, clean and has marine biologists on board giving great information and collecting data.. Well worth the trip as was a day trip to Salem if you have time...A CIty trolly tour is a must when you first arrive to get an idea of what is where and some history. I would recomment the Red Sox one as it covers a larger area, it depends how much time you have. You can get on and off the trolly all day, you do not have to stay on for a whole tour.We will definitely stay there again when we are next in Boston

<Author>BPK_Travel
<Content>Great Hotel, Excellent Location This hotel has THE BEST location in all of Boston. It's right across the street from Boston Common, the Public Garden, the Capitol, and a short 2-3 block walk to Fanueil Hall, Quincy Market, and downtown crossing. It's about a 10 minute walk to Boston's North End, where some of the best restaurants are located. When you're tired of walking, you can jump on one of Boston's many subway lines (aka the T). This hotel is located near Park St., Downtown Crossing, and Government Center, which makes it easy to get on any subway line without having to transfer. The hotel is very classic/contemporary and has a welcoming, comfortable feel to it. Upon entering there's a nice sitting area where they have complimentary happy hour in the evening. The staff was nice, friendly, and outgoing. They made me feel at home while on the road. The rooms were clean, well laid out, and had enough pictures and decor that didn't make it feel like a normal hotel room. It was not noisy given the downtown location. This hotel helped me maximize my time while on the road and also allowed me to enjoy my time in Boston. I highly recommend the Nine Zero and look forward to coming back.

<Author>cattails121
<Content>Good and satisfying stay We stayed at the Nine Zero Hotel to attend a commencement ceremony in Boston. The hotel is a few steps away from the subway (Park St station, Red and Green line), and close to Boston Commons. Area is also safe (we came back late at around 10-11pm every night).About the hotel : we reserved our room through the hotel website, which gave a much cheaper rate than if you called the hotel directly. On the website, it asked whether you want 'higher floor, or lower', and whether you want 'feather pillows or foam'. We asked for a room on the higher floor, and feather pillows, and both requests were accommodated when we arrived. We were given a room on the 18th floor, with a beautiful view of the State House. Pillows and bed are very comfortable. Sheets are very clean. Hotel has a chic feel, smells nice as soon as you walk in. The interior decor of the room and the hotel can be interpreted as either stylish or tacky, but these are not major issues for me as I much prefer hotel to be clean, which the Nine Zero is. We also used the hotel gym, and although it is rather on the small side, it is functional, clean, doesn't smell, and it has good equipment. One thing we really liked was the in-room safe which is designed to accommodate laptop computers. We put our two laptop computers in it everytime we went out. Some issues : 1) housekeeping didn't replenish the body soap when they cleaned our room. We wondered whether they forgot about it. No big deal. When we came back from walking around Boston that night, we just stopped at the front desk to ask for soap, and they readily accommodated us, and even asked whether they should call housekeeping to replenish us with more. Very professional and accommodating.2) Second issue : On the brochure in the room itself, it stated that there's 'complimentary coffee' somewhere in the hotel (I forgot where, lobby perhaps), but when I called front desk to inquire about it, they said they don't have complimentary coffee, but coffee could be bought at the hotel restaurant. Hmmm. If you don't have it, then don't say it on the brochure ! Probably they changed the policy, which is fine, but the info given to customers in the brochures should be updated as well. Oh, by the way, room doesn't come with coffee maker or coffee, but they do have margarita mix !All in all, it was a very good and very satisfying stay. Staff is professional and friendly. Nine Zero tends to be on the expensive side (we paid around $375 per night for our room), but the hotel is nice, clean, with comfortable bed and pillows, clean towels, crisp sheets, very close to subway. There's Dunkin Donuts and Finagle Bagel a block away for your morning coffee and breakfast. We would definitely stay here again.

<Author>Peter_Smallhill
<Content>Very nice but watch out for street noise Very friendly and helpful staff. No snobbery. Also, for a boutique hotel, interior decoration is rather understated rather than artsy-fartsy, which creates a pleasant low-key atmosphere.Rooms are very functional, and include extremely comfortable bedding and good quality amenities.However, when you book, if you are sensitive to noise book on an upper floor. Street noise on lower floors is a real problem because the rooms are not sound proofed and there are noisy garbage trucks operating around 3-4 AM some nights. ( Also, neighboring TV can be heard sometimes.) The upper floors also have nice views whereas the lower floors have no view at all. They book you in a lower floor room unless you make this request.Location is excellent for a walking tour. Paul Revere's grave along with other early patriots is right across the street!

<Author>spyglassweb
<Content>Great Service The best thing about Nine Zero is the service. From the bell service to room service to the front desk, every experience was excellent. Also the location is great for a business trip.The rooms are very clean and stocked with Mario Badescu beauty products (shampoo, etc). Also the robe is a nice touch.The only thing I didn't care for was the decor. To me, it looked like a tacky, garish modern interpretation of the Art Deco style. The bed cover was black and tan wide stripes...ugh. The chair in the room looked like it belonged in a clowns room, with its ridiculously high back. Way too much laminated black furniture! Also, in the areas outside the elevators there is tacky shimmery bronze lamae curtains covering the walls. This is just not my preference, as I prefer a more understated atmosphere. Others I was traveling with, loved the decor. The bathroom was nice, in all white tile and marble, very different in style from the rest of the room.I enjoyed the service, but since ambiance is important to me, I will look for a different hotel next time I am in Boston.

<Author>sben123
<Content>My new favorite place to stay in Boston.... I recently stayed at Nine Zero during a business trip and was very pleased. Prior to check in, I requested a higher floor room of which I was upgraded to upon check in. The hotel has a free cocktail reception in the lobby from 5-6pm and is worth checking out. They also have free coffee in the morning in a to go cup in the restaurant hotel on the 2nd floor. The room is of average size and modern (a little larger than another Kimpton I stayed in). The shower and bed are amazing. Nine Zero really puts care into every detail (in room chocolates upon arrival, use of robes, fully stocked mini bar with martini bar (fee) and a complimentary CD to listen in the room). I ordered room service for dinner and had the Nine Zero Burger and lobster bisque (both delicious, but a bit expensive). The hotel staff was very friendly and patient. They helped me print several copies that I needed for a meeting and didn't charge me for it. The hotel staff including Thomas Burke was extremely kind and helpful about advice on places to eat and things to do in my short stay. Overall, a wonderful stay and I would highly recommend the hotel to others.

<Author>AntoniaB
<Content>Slighty down at heel for a 5* hotel I was expecting great things from this hotel having read the glowing reviews on Trip Advisor but felt slightly disappointed with the room in particularI can't fault the staff: courteous and friendly (like all Bostonians!) but the room was a bit down at heel. It was a large room with two beds in it on the 7th floor but the view was off a back alley and there was construction work going on - although not much the hotel can do, it was quite noisy. The beds were, as everyone else testifies to, extremely comfortable with soft linen and to die for pillows/duvet so a good sleep is guaranteed. However, the sheet on my bed had a big hole in it, which i wouldn't expect of any hotel, let alone a 5* star one. There were also black scuff marks along the walls. I would have thought staff would have tried to get rid of these...!Also, Kimpton Hotel Group (owners of Nine Zero) claim to be very considerate of the environment and ask that you reuse your towels rather than have them replaced every day, which we duly tried to but the maids kept replacing them with new ones!We hired a couple of in room films, which at 拢5 each wasnt too bad and they were all very current (some not out in the UK) but there is a huge cinema just a couple of blocks away. As someone else said in room food is damn expensive by the time you've added on a service charge and tax.Having said all that, it's a very central hotel, great for accessing the Freedom Trail and the shops (go to Newbury st for great boutique shops!), and I would stay again so it certainly wasn't a bad experience. Oh, and they have a 'drinks reception' at 5pm every day - free wine, which can't be sniffed at. If you want to get out for a drink there is a good bar with great food called Silvertone just one or two streets down from the hotel (matthew mcconeghy was filming there when we stayed!). it might be worth upgrading to a suite when you're there (if you can afford it). We gota v good deal with Expedia - return flights from Scotland and 4 nights in nine zero for 拢500 - so shop around.

<Author>edinweegie
<Content>An average hotel. We stayed here for 3 nights en route to New England for a skiing holiday, and overall, it was okay. I'm probably a little disappointed in it and maybe had higher expectations based on the reviews here. The hotel is modern, but the room we had was a little small, a little scuffed round the edges, had a lot of traffic noise, had a Queen bed rather than a King and did not have a bath tub, only a shower. The lack of bath probably wouldn't bother some people, but as we were doing a lot of walking/sightseeing and fancied a soak to rejuvenate the feet and legs, we asked for a room with a tub after the first night. The staff were very good and immediately changed us to a slightly higher floor room, with a tub, and strangely about twice the space although the room types were supposedly the same. This room actually proved to be much better and was quiet as it was at the back of the hotel. Unfortunately as someone else pointed out, as it was low down it was actually dark the whole day, even on the glorious sunny days that we had. The safe in this room was locked when we got in, so we asked for it to be opened for us and the staff said it would be done right away. It wasn't. We asked again the next day and were told again it would be done. After coming back to the room late that night, we found it still hadn't been done. No big deal, but as we were checking out the next day, it wasn't worth asking again.On the plus side, the staff are genuinely pleasant, the location is really good, the wine reception is a nice touch and the hotel offers free wi-fi. There was nothing that bad about the hotel and nothing that great either. It is a little too focused on style, and while the staff are pleasant, the service is a little hit or miss. Based on this visit, I wouldn't stay at Nine Zero again.

<Author>holsworthy
<Content>Boston is great I stayed at the Nine Zero for 4 nights in February half term with my 15 year old daughter hotel is great very luxurious rooms are a dream. The room service and over all service given by staff is brilliant scott the concierge is very efficient. The only negative experience was at the end of a long sightseeing day we went to the bar for a glass of wine (soft drink for daughter!) I stood for 1 hour waiting to be served and was completely ignored and I left without a drink! The bar is on 2nd floor pitch black rather like a nightclub than hotel bar and was not at all welcoming I felt that your face had to fit! and its seemed mine did not. The location is ok for sights seeing you can pick up the trolley tour really close the freedom trail is on the doorstep but there are not many places to eat in vicinity of the hotel expecially for people travelling with children unless you want dunkin donuts or burger king I did not! The old town trolley tour was fantastic value hop on hop off all day long and the tour guide big Al was good fun even though we were only two people on his tour. If I could advise anyone Id say go to Boston in spring the parks will be lovely and all attractions will be open which is the one thing we found a lot of things dont open till late March but we had fab time and would go again.

<Author>CLB27
<Content>Clean and comfy I only stayed here for a night, but it was a really nice hotel. I would definitely recommend it to others. The location is great - right around the corner from Downtown Crossing, close the theater district, close to china town, close to beacon hill and Boston common and within a mile to Fanueil Hall and the TD Banknorth Garden. Lots of great things within walking distance. The hotel itself has funky modern decor, which was fun. The rooms were a decent size with extremely comfy beds and were nice and clean. The bathroom was decent too, all marble and looked very clean. There was a decent sized closet, which contained a bathrobe, slipper socks (to purchase) an umbrella, etc. The minibar was tempting but ridiculously expensive (no shock there). The restaurant was far too pricey for my liking, but there was a decent pub next door with good nachos, drinks and good music. One complaint: I called for directions on the way into Boston, which were fine, except the receptionist told me that the valet parking enterance was on Broomfield St, which was a one way street, we were unable to turn onto. So we spent a half hour trying to maneuver the busy one was streets, only to find out it was the wrong street altogether! The valet enterance was actually on Bosworth St. Talk about a bit of frustration, though we eventually figured it out. Regardless, given the opportunity, I would go back.

<Content>Nine Zero a hip mid-Boston refuge I spent 2 very pleasant days in a 16th floor (upgraded view) Queen room. Design  decor touches are evident everywhere in the hotel. <Content>A Wonderful Experience At Nine Zero My husband and I stayed at this hotel for three nights. We drove through a blinding snowstorm New Years Day for 4 and 1/2 hours and arrived as you can imagine pretty worn out. From the first moment until our check out the hotel staff did everything to make our stay relaxing and memorable. Our room, a high floor with a terrific view of the skyline, was spacious, especially for a large city hotel (we're used to the shoe boxes we stay in for twice the price in New York). The whole atmosphere is classy but not pretentious. We had been vactioning in Maine, skiing and hiking, and we felt completely comfortable at Nine Zero in our jeans and sweaters. The evening wine reception is a nice touch. The housekeeping staff was so accomodating with a coffee pot and extra pillows. The front desk was so helpful, right down to printing our boarding passes for our flight home. The restaurants recommended to us were all universally terrific. Just the right feel for our casual vacation. I would recommend this hotel for a romantic get away or celebration as it never felt stuffy - just fun. Great design, great staff. A terrific experience.

<Author>TD60
<Content>A wonderful city hotel in downtown Boston. My wife and I just returned from weekend getaway at the Nine Zero in Boston.Hotel and Location: The Nine Zero is a deluxe boutique hotel located near the northeast corner of Boston Common adjacent to the Freedom Trail. The Nine Zero is within walking distance of the Public Garden, the Government Center, the Theater District, Faneuil Hall, the North End (Little Italy) and downtown restaurants, shopping and nightlife. There's also a nearby T (subway) station about a block away. We found the hotel to be so conveniently located that once we handed our car keys to the valet at check-in, we didn't need them again until we checked out. The hotel's somewhat minimalist decor can best be described as urban chic. The hotel offers complementary wine tastings nightly in the hotel lobby, which is a fantastic amenity. The Nine Zero's well-trained staff is very professional, gracious and accommodating.Room: As a Kimpton in Touch member I got a very reasonable One Day Sale rate of $209 for a King Premier Room (compared to the $279 weekend rack rate). I must admit that due to the territory-marking behavior of dogs I was skeptical of staying at a pet-friendly property, but my concerns were unfounded. The room was very clean and stylishly decorated. The extremely comfortable king-sized bed had plush linens, a warm down comforter and the softest down pillows we鈥檝e ever slept on. The marble bathroom was very nice and my wife loved the hotel鈥檚 deluxe toiletries. The room and bathroom were more spacious than most standard city hotel rooms. Among the many appreciated in-room amenities were chocolate truffles and raspberries at nightly turndown. For those travelling on business, there's free high speed Internet and wireless connectivity in each room. Dining: We had dinner at KO Prime, an innovative steakhouse located on the hotel's second floor. KO Prime is an extraordinary restaurant named after renowned Executive Chef Ken Oringer (formally of the Boston Eliot Hotel's Mobil 4-Star restaurant Clio). The appetizers, sides, entrees and desserts were all delicious, portions were generous, the service and presentation were superb and the wine list was impressive. The restaurant's hip atmosphere was trendy but refined. Like most fine restaurants, KO Prime is somewhat pricey - plan on spending $100 per person for a four-course dinner not including wine (if you order the Kobe Beef, plan on spending at least twice that per person). Most of the reds on the wine list were priced between $100 to $150 per bottle (there were few offerings below that). In fact, my only complaint about the restaurant is that the wine list markup seemed excessive to me. (I have a small wine cellar at home consisting mainly of Barolo, Barbaresco and red Bordeaux, so I consider myself to be pretty good at cherry picking limited-production/good value reds off of restaurant wine lists). These days, I can usually find a very good/delicious 1996-2001 Barolo or Barbaresco or Cru Classe Bordeaux from a better producer for around $80, which I consider to be a relatively good value at finer restaurants. Unfortunately, I was unable to find a good value at that price point on KO Prime's wine list. Despite this, KO Prime is definitely worth visiting for a special occasion.Overall, the Nine Zero is a wonderful city hotel in a great location... The One Day Sale rate of $209 was also a great value... We'd definitely stay here again!

I was not at all disappointed in the service which was excellent but the hotel was, at best, nothing to write home about. <Author>pattikwestfield
<Content>Location and Service My husband and I spent one night at the Nine Zero while visiting our son in Boston. We'd stayed at the hotel several times before it became a Kimpton property and we were just as impressed now as we were before. The staff is extremely professional and courteous and nothing is too much for them to do. The location of the hotel could not be better - perfect for stepping out and sight-seeing. Woke up to a beautiful morning and walked through the Public Gardens and the Commons - it was just a wonderful way to begin a day. My only complaints had to do with housekeeping - some dust issues, dirty grout in areas of the shower, metal tissue box holder not cleaned, ironing board left out at turn-down service, no cups in the bathroom for use, no shower cap, I feel the standards for housekeeping should be higher at such a beautiful property. To end on a high note, the beds were extremely comfortable and I will be purchasing some pillows from the hotel site soon! All in all, we're always happy to stay at the Nine Zero and hopefully the housekeeping kinks will be worked out. AND - much to our surprise, as returning guests parking was complimentary. Now that was a nice touch!

<Author>Georgester
<Content>High expectations, but disappointed Given the rave reviews this hotel had recieved I had high expectations of what it would offer. The rooms are well styled (comfy bed, nice furnishings), although a little tired around the edges (curtain was frayed). There was no bath in the the bathroom - apparently only 10% of the rooms have baths. And there are no coffee machines either - these are available only on request as I found out (so not sure what those nice coffee machines are doing on their website!). My room service meal was also forgotten about. On the positive side, the restaurant for breakfast was excellent - the service quick and attentive (although this was at 6.30am, so perhaps a little early for most people). Style wise, this is definitely more pleasing than the usual impersonal hotel, but given it calls itself a 'boutique' hotel (and a price to match) overall I was disappointed.

<Author>willSA
<Content>Nine Zero Good Hotel in Great Location Reviewer: A Trip Advisor member from San Antonio, Texas.Family of three (son age 14) stayed 8/11/07-8/15/07. Had reserved standard double queen room (summer special $309 rate), but as a Kimpton in Touch member, upon check-in, we received a free upgrade to a deluxe room with a view on a higher floor. Hotel is very modern in design and execution and is quite attractive throughout. Best of all is the location --adjacent to Boston Common right on the Freedom Trail and only a block from the subway. Hotel staff was very friendly and helpful--particularly at the concierge desk. The stay was not without a couple of problems, however. The modern design of the bathroom--and the glass shower in particular--was a problem, in that the shower door leaked water on to the floor and had to be fixed. Also, several channels on the Direct TV feed froze, and required a call to get them working. Finally, the hotel's highly praised restaurant just recently closed--it changed names and format (the previous chef left to open his own reataurant), and the new menu and prices did not look good enough to attract us for dinner. The one breakfast we had there was good, but overpriced. All in all, we really like Kimpton Hotels--the style, the amenities and the people. I recommend the Nine Zero.

<Author>gothamfoodie
<Content>Great Experiences at Nine Zero This hotel really delivers on its promise of luxury, great service and quiet, elegant rooms. The location is perfectly central (and right on the freedom trail) and a block from a T stop. My husband and I stayed for 4 days to celebrate our anniversary. The hotel is very chic and clean and the service was always very friendly - no attitudes here. Many business travelers stay at the NZ. We were shown our room which was on the 8th floor and was very neat and stylish. The rooms are not huge, but storage is ample and the beds, linens and pillows are heavenly. The TV and wardrobe cabinets are recessed into the wall. The design of the rooms is casual but luxurious. Baths are divine as are the toiletries (Mario Russo). Right after we unpacked, we noticed that our bathroom sporatically gave off an offensive sewage smell. we phoned the front desk and they sent someone up right away and moved us to the top floor. Wow! the windows on the top 4 floors are essentially wall-to-wall and floor-to-ceiling. same layout, but the views are incredible. You can see from Beacon Hill to the river and all the way to the Back Bay and Boston Common. views of the state house at night are gorgeous too.We were sent a fruit and cheese plate and a bottle of wine to apologize for our smelly first room. Concierge is very helpful. We didn't experience anything negative during our stay other than the temporary stinky bathroom which was dealt with quicklyand efficiently. Will definitely recommend this hotel and stay again.

<Author>lilydiva1
<Content>Mixed Experience I read others' reviews of this hotel on this site and was looking forward to spending two nights here while I was in Boston on business. Some things about the hotel were great -- the night I arrived, for example, I did not get to the hotel until 1:30 am and had not had dinner -- room service quickly brought me sandwich and a pot of tea and I was grateful! Their internet access was excellent, wake-up calls flawless, and their staff was invariably polite. The room was comfortable, with many nice amenities and extras, including a CD player. I liked the decor a lot. Their express dry cleaning service was super.A few negative experiences, however: (1) The room was not as clean as it should have been, particularly the bathroom -- it did not meet the standards of a standard business class hotel like a Hilton or Hyatt. The walls were dirty, the sink and floor in the bathroom had splotches and sticky patches, the drinking glasses were dirty, the upholstery and carpet had spots and stains, and the bathrobes were frayed and worn; (2) On the second morning, I ordered a french omelette off their room service menu, as I had done the day before. Twenty minutes later, I got a call from room service asking me what the ingredients were for a french omelette. I told the person that I wasn't sure exactly but didn't they know since it was on their menu? She told me that the french omelette was not on their menu. I told her that I had ordered the same thing the day before from their menu, which was sitting in front of me! 45 minutes after I initially ordered, my french omelette did arrive -- and was delicious as usual -- but this was an annoying interlude on a busy morning; (3) Both mornings, the housekeeper knocked once on my door and before I could get to the door to see who it was, had unlocked the door and entered my room (this is not reassuring for women traveling alone); (4) There were errors on my bill which had to be ironed out -- a valet parking charge when I didn't even have a car. To their credit, they rectified the situation quickly and politely -- but it was time-consuming. Bottom line -- the hotel was comfortable and the staff was polite and friendly, but no hotel can lose sight of the basics: cleanliness and a well-trained staff.

<Author>TwoAmps
<Content>Great location, great service, great views possible, great staff... Great hotel (but it should be great for the price--when did a good big-city hotel room get to be 4-something a night? I missed that memo...). Wonderful staff. The concierge did what concierges are supposed to be able to do--make good tables appear at great restaurants that we wouldn't have thought of otherwise, the valets knew foolproof (important in Boston) shortcuts to anywhere we wanted to go, and overall, it just felt like the machine was really running well. Even at the high-end, the rooms aren't exactly huge with a single King, and would be really packed, as reported elsewhere, with two Queens. Closet space is at a premium, with the safe, a big drawer, and the ironing stuff taking up a lot of room. we had trouble finding room for 4 days worth of coats and clothes for two. We did like the comfy-modern decor, and the views from the upper floor rooms, with the floor-to-ceiling windows, can be pretty jaw-dropping. (chatting with someone at the University (I think it's a law school) across the street, he pointed out that the views IN those big windows can be pretty jaw-dropping, too. This isn't the only building on the block with 19 floors, and that ain't one-way glass, folks...)

<Author>jatallah
<Content>Not worth the money This is a swanky, small hotel. The ratings are good enough. They've acquired enough awards and accolades. The location is fantastic for the leisure traveler wanting to walk Boston--you can hop on the Freedom Trail just outside. The rooms are nicely appointed with European sheets, robe, and spa items from Mario Russo. The staff was helpful in loading/unloading, check-in, concierge services and calling transportation.What is not good? THE BEDS ARE OLD. You can have the finest linens in the world, but it will never mask a worn-out bed. My husband and I had a queen and neither of us got a full night's sleep on any of the four nights we stayed. We left our vacation feeling more tired than when we arrived.Second, THE ROOM SERVICE IS TERRIBLE. On two mornings we ordered from from the room service menu. On a continental breakfast, they forgot the juice both times, neglected salt/peppper, butter for toast and breads, and sugar for our tea and coffee. They were out of an offered yogurt for our entire length of stay. The second morningn they sent a completely different meal from what my husband ordered! They did make it right, but at a hotel of this advertised calibur, the service could be 100x better. We did not even dare enter the restaurant, Spire, for that reason.Also, be advised with the pampering service, this means they enter your room about 3x a day. Once in the a.m. for cleaning, once in the afternoon and once for turndown. If you want more privacy, let them know, rather than shooing housekeeping three times in a day, as we had to do.

<Author>Fintraveller
<Content>Unfortunately a disappointment a second time aroung This was my second time at the Nine Zero. My first time was in August and I was so excited about the hotel that I recommended it to our company's travel and event services. Everything (except the extremely poor service in the Spire restaurant) was excellent. I couldn't wait to go back! And I do not say this lightly - I'm a very seasoned traveller and have over 50 hotel nights per year. This is not a cheap place (I paid $400 per night, but it was worth it).So, with great expectations I returned in October. I'm a very light sleeper so my assistant had requested a quiet room on a high floor. (And last time it worked perfectly). Not such luck this time although thispreference is also clearly stated in my Kimpton frequent quest profile. I was given a room 1502 - high floor, but so much street noise that I had 3 very poorly slept nights. The housekeeping, which as impeccable last time, left a lot of room for improvement this time around: the empty shower gel bottle stood in the shower for 3 days and a new one was not provided until I called and requested one (most annoying when you're wet in the shower already and notice this). The sheets were so worn that there literally was a hole in it! You would expect this in a cheap budget hotel but not in a place like Nine Zero...Then the room service. On both mornings I ordered a big pot of green tea. On the first day the pot of hot water came with 8 tea bags (which was a bit excessive, but at least enough) on the second morning I just got one (with a big pot of water and with at $10 price tag not quite what I expected). When I requested a second tea bag from the waitress, I was told that I can have one only if I pay extra ($5). Granted, I'm on an expense account and it doesn't matter, but this kind of greediness gives a very poor overall impression of the hotel's mentality.And about the Spire restaurant; the menu had 3 seafood choices (I don't eat meat) of which 2 were sold out. What was most annoying was that we were not told about this in the beginning, but only after we had already made our selections. At that point the waitress told us: Oh, we don't have that anymore tonight. No, that neither.Overall my second visit didn't meet my expectations, but that might've been partly do to the fact that the hotel seemed to be fully booked., which was not the case during my first visit.Let's hope they'll get their act together since this place really has a lot of potential!

<Author>KateKirk
<Content>Great location, low on biz traveler standards I seek out Kimpton Hotels for their stylishness and great locations in major U.S. cities. Nine Zero hits most marks for friendly staff, wonderfully comfortable rooms (oh those sheets...), chic local brand toiletries, a great Tremont Street location and a swanky bar/restaurant, but for $400 a night, I expect a little bit more catering to the weary business traveler. Coffee is offered but it's not out until 7 am (on a weekend that's ok), the desk is completely unworkable for a laptop, and the fitness center was really subpar...rickety equipment, no television, a door that sits open rather than being keyed...not my idea of security when you are a woman working out alone at 5 am. It's the little things that really matter when you have to be away from home for work and I think Nine Zero could work on it. I did enjoy a fantastic view of the Charles River, Fenway and other sites from my 19th floor room....really spectacular.

<Content>Wonderful Hotel! my husband and i stayed at the nine zero for three nights earlier this month...we were very happy with our entire stay. the staff was one of the nicest we have ever encountered in all of our hotel stays and we do alot of travel. the hotel is small but intimate with a private feel. you never see many people in the lobby ...it is quiet and calm. we stayed in a corner view room on the 14th floor and had an amazing view, the windows were huge and it had a really wonderful urban feel. the room was spaced nicely even though it was not big. the matress was the best one i have slept on in a long time including just about every 5 star hotel. the linens were wonderful, clean crisp and white with great pillows. we were greated with a fruit plate and coffee as we arrived early in the morning. it was so nice to check in early with no questions asked. the room had a great choice of magazines and daily newspapers. the spiro restaurant was an excellant place for drinks and a snack. nice atmosphere. we also had a few fabulous breakfasts there. my only complaint was of the young bartenders behind the second floor bar at night. both during room service and at the spiro bar itself they were cold and did not know anything about the wines they had in stock, nor did they care to find out. it seemed as if they were bored students just making their buck , it supprised me that this would be the case since everyone else in the entire hotel was excellent...in spite of that we still had a nice time while we were there. Akeem and Thomas were EXTREMELY EXCEPTIONAL front house workers...anything you wanted they would help you with ( and with a real smile, not some phony yes sir or yes mame service.) the location cant be beat. its right next to park and a 5 min T ride to airport or a 10 min cab ride to airport. lots of great shopping and restaurants nearby and accross the park. the free internet access was a nice touch as well as the wine happy hour which we seemed to keep missing. the hotel had somewhat of a W feel but a much much nicer staff and cozier feel. we will definitely be back and will try out the other kimptons.

<Author>remymartin11
<Content>Like a W Hotel, with a much friendlier staff My boyfriend and I stayed at Nine Zero (a Kimpton Hotel) in Boston for one night on Aug. 27th. The furniture and design of the hotel reminded us very much of a W Hotel. The staff was amazingly friendly at every turn. The location was the best you can get in Boston if you are doing the tourist thing (right across the street from the Old Granary Burial Ground, close to the beginning of the Freedom Trail).There was a wine tasting in the lobby from 5-7pm, that apparently takes place every night and featured tasty wine (not cheap-tasting bar wine). It really added to the friendly atmosphere of the hotel and there were many strangers interacting with each other, which you rarely see in a hotel lobby. If I traveled much for my job, I would make sure to stay at a Kimpton hotel whenever possible. They really make it homey and have nice touches, such as bathrobes, slippers, umbrellas, free internet (which was very slow, by the way), etc. along with a great price (we paid $179 for the one night).

<Author>njsuburbian
<Content>Excellent Location, Great Hotel, Good Staff The hotel is a very trendy hotel and is in a great location. We walked everywhere during our stay. Even Fenway and the Prudential Center are only a 15 minute walk. Quincy Market is 3 Blocks away and Boston Common is literally across the street. The rooms are a decent size. They aren't small, but they aren't tiny. The beds are very comfortable as well as the other furniture. The staff is good as well. The concierge there, Steven, was very helpful in providing help for a myriad of different requests. I saw him sit down with a person for practically 30 minutes and plan out her entire weeklong vacation with numerous reservations and other requests without even showing a negative look on his face.There are a few downsides to staying in the hotel:- Parking is $35 a day and isn't on-site (it's a valet service)- For a 4-star hotel there is no doorman- The valet entrance with the bell-hops is on the side and it's very hard to manuver cars in the small side street. There is no stopping on Tremont St. in front of the hotel-The staff didn't seem to be very organized, however whenever anything went wrong, they were very helpful and without a doubt, the staff tried their hardest to make each and every customer's stay a positive one.

<Author>tonikeb
<Content>Great hotel in a Great location! The Nine Zero is a modern boutique hotel located in downtown Boston. The outside of the hotel is brick and looks like a lot of the other buildings in this city. However, its insides are quite modern and sleek making for an enjoyable contrast in such a historic town.The hotel is located on the Freedom Trail directly across the street from the very old Granary Cemetary. Paul Revere, Samuel Adams, and the parents of Benjamin Franklin (among others) are buried there. Our corner room allowed us a terrific people watching view, including the groups taking tours led by people dressed in revolutionary period clothing. Boston is known as a walking city and almost everything is within walking distance from this hotel. The financial district is in one direction and the theater district in another. One edge of Boston Common (the furthest side from the Public Garden) is 1block away to the south. You can choose from high end stores and dining on Newbury Street at the end of the Public Garden or find moderate shopping and fast food on Washinton Street, which is one city block to the east of Nine Zero.The Park Street T (subway) station is only 1 block away, too. Both the red line and green line trains can be taken from this station for $1.25 per person per ride. The red line (outbound) will take you over to Cambridge and the green line will take you to Fenway Park or up to the North End. You could also transfer from the green line to the blue line, which takes you to the wharf. Don't panic if this sounds complicated. It's not! The friendly and very helpful concierge at the hotel provided us with a clearly marked map and very easy to follow directions. The decor of this hotel is modern. Our room was nicely sized and the bed was wonderfully comfortable. The bath was stocked with Mario Russo (a local salon) products. The sea salt soap is divine!! Our room was so comfortable we decided to have dinner via room service one night. It was delivered hot  quickly and it was delicious. Note: When we were calling to place our dinner order, the line to room service rang a few times so the call was automatically routed to the front desk. Instead of trying to transfer us back to that line, the front desk person took our order! This was a very nice customer service touch.The only quirk to the Nine Zero hotel is finding a few items tucked into dresser drawers. We discovered our coffee maker in one drawer after already grabbing some coffee from Starbucks around the corner. Also, housekeeping came by bright and early on a Saturday morning but we didn't find our do not disturb hanger (in another drawer) until a day too late. Very, very minor for an otherwise outstanding stay.I would definitely stay at the Nine Zero again.  
<Date>Jun 12, 2006

<Author>Twinkler
<Content>Great Trendy Location The fantastic Nine Zero hotel is located in the heart of the city. Just steps from Boston Common. The nearby Trolley stops are very close and will run about 25.00USD for a jump on jump off pass. The hotel is super trendy and some may feel over powered by its sheer moderness. However most find this hotel to be a good value and very clean. I stayed personally at this hotel last year and loved every minuet of it. The front desk staff is very helpful and kind. The onsite manager is very helpful.The hotels staff is more than willing to help you find nearby attractions such as Cheers, Fenway Park, Freedom Trail, Fleet Center or the New England Aquarium.The hotel also has a fantastic upscale eatery called Spire. Spire can be quite expensive, but well worth the money. I apple martini will run you about 12.50USD. The hotel provides a wide range of deserts. Please do not expect to sit in the eatery and expect to just have desert, you will be asked to move to the bar area. Since the hotel is located centrally hailing a cab is no problem. The hotel is also only about a 20 minuet cab ride from Logan International Airport. The big dig or the massive construction effort sometimes slows this time down. I would recommend asking for a room as high up as possible. The views are amazing and majestic. Boston is a fantastic city and Nine Zero is an ideal place to stay for business or personal travel. Hotel does not offer many things to keep children busy.

<Author>Roadtravlr
<Content>Trendy and Friendly...with Hidden Charges! Ninezero was trendy, and friendly. The reception desk and rest of hotel staff met you with warm greetings and even remembered names! The location is pretty good for staying in the Boston city-center--you are near at least 2 T stations by foot, gov't center station and park street station (no less than a seven minute walk from either) and there are things to see and do in the area (I highly recommend taking the Black Heritage Tour given by the National Park Service rangers--a great walk around historic Beacon Hill and engaging tour of the city's rich civil war history). However, it had a lot of hidden charges. They charge you for a double room but do not explain to you it is not a one time only fee. They put colorful drinks outside of the bar, but will charge you like it was from inside the bar if you touch it. They put beautiful gifts around the room and charge outrageous prices for it (e.g., a bath stuffs bag with the normal size bottles of the small bathroom products...$91!). The food at the hotel's restaraunt, Spire, was pretty good. I ordered room service and while it was all pricey, i must admit they don't skimp on the portion size at all. I actually went to Spire for breakfast before checking out and it was a bit pricey but really good and very filling--i couldn't finish it.This hotel is for adults that read the fine print. Not for children that want to play around with out spending allot of cash (read: young adults that want to experience the lap of luxury, if ever-so briefly) . It is trendy and for the rich and famous. Thus, they are looking to wine, dine, and stick you for your pesos.

<Author>Shton1
<Content>Excellent Service, Very Nice Rooms I stayed at the Nine Zero with 5 other friends for 3 nights two weekends ago. We had 3 rooms and I chose the hotel partly for its location, although everything seems pretty close in Boston, and also partly because of the accolades the hotel has received from various travel magazines. The rooms at Nine Zero are quite nice if you like contemporary decor. The beds were incredibly comfortable, although the pillows were a little soft for my taste. I also liked the color schemes of the rooms with bright yellows and reds accenting the almost black mahogany furniture. I was placed in a Spectacular room on the 17th floor with nice skyline views. The bathrooms are spacious, with nice bath ammenities. One of my biggest pet peeves is showers with low water pressure, I was quite pleased with the copious water pressure and plentiful hot water at the Nine Zero. One other thing that would probably make this hotel even more desirable for the business traveler is the oversized work desk with ergonomic office chair and high-speed internet access in the room. While the rooms were certainly nice, the staff really sets the hotel apart. Every interaction with all of the staff from check-in to check-out was quite pleasant. Fatima at the front desk and all of the doormen/valets derserve special kudos for treating my group like VIP's. The doormen were amazing in getting us transportation anywhere we needed to go at a moment's notice, including a private car to Fenway Park on a game day. We only had one meal at the restaurant, but it was very good and the prices were comprable to hotels in this class. I would recommend this hotel without hesitation to anyone looking for nice accomodations and professional service.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent service, good handicapped bathroom, great bed The service was excellent. The restaurant serves an very good breakfast as well. The bed was incredibly comfortable; it may be the best hotel bed that I've ever slept in. I am in a wheelchair, and the handicapped bathroom is well designed. I did expect the main room to be a little larger, but it did not impair my ability to move around the room to access the bed nearest the door, the desk, and the entertainment unit. I only could not get to the window, which would have made a difference were I alone and needing to open or close the blinds. Their blinds are also excellent for keeping out light if you are something of a late sleeper, as I am. The location of the hotel is fantastic. It's in the middle of the city with a historic graveyard just across the street, where Paul Revere, Samuel Adams, and many of Ben Franklin's family members are buried. You can wander for five minutes in any direction and reach something enjoyable or significant. Boston Commons is not far away.I had a great trip to Boston, and the hotel was part of the reason.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Stylishly Uncomfortable Pros- Near a redline T stop (very convenient)- Near Boston Common and multiple historical areas- Generally nice and friendly staff- Nice, cute bathroom amenities (though less available in standard rooms)- Everything new and sparlkingCons- Many features of the room designed for style not comfort or function- Weak (though free) hi-fi, poor overall on anything technical- Rooms are on the small side- Standard rooms lack bathtub- Area gets pretty sketchy at nightI'd heard through the locals and read that Nine Zero was THE new hip and trendy hotel in Boston. That is most certainly the case. During our stay, Louis Farrahkan (and a huge entourage) as well as the Black Eyed Peas, also stayed here. The hotel was definitely buzzing. Nonetheless, the staff stayed on top of their game throughout the week - always polite and efficient and even quite friendly. That much was fun. Only exception was when we tried to get a DVD player they brushed us off, eventually admitting there is only one in the hotel and it was lent out indefinitely. When I called again the next day and asked about a wait list I was discouraged from this and then told I probably wouldn't want it anyway since it was attached to a 13 inch television. We were far from impressed by the overall tech features of this hotel, even though it tries to brand itself as being high tech. More on that below.The rooms, however, are a royal pain. The beds are very comfy, and that's vital for me in any hotel stay (a main reason I steer clear of most Marriotts nowadays). Unfortunately, many details are either inconvenient or just plain nonfunctioinal. For example, you simply cannot turn on the shower without getting your face, shoulder and arm blasted with cold water. This is in addition to a very cool looking sliding barn door on the bathroom that will slam your fingers if you're not paying attention. I thought I was just an idiot when I did this so didn't mention it to my boyfriend and he ended up slamming his hand in the door later that day. Also, there are no towel racks. After four days of staying here, I finally improvised a towel rack above the toilet, but housekeeping steathily removed and corrected these attempts, folding and replacing the towels below the sink, where they were unreachable from the shower. Another annoying feature - while they do have free wi-fi, it's very spotty. My boyfriend kept cursing every time he got booted. I got frustrated at the waxing and waning of the connection - you developed a rushed mentality whenever a strong signal appeared and tried to get everything done. This was compounded by the fact that there are no electrical outlets near the bed. Since my boyfriend was constantly at the desk working, god bless his productive soul, and the arm chair was unattractively squashed into the corner, the only other place to use your computer was on the bed. I had to constantly try to remember to plug my laptop back in to juice up the battery. Since we're locals (ousted by renovations), things like our gym being nearby and a big movie complex are great. Btw, the gym here is subpar for a nice new hotel. The SCLA is down the block, attached to the Ritz, and the nicest gym in Boston. Not cheap, but excellent facilities.The climate control, as I mentioned above, is not very precise. It is not digital and when it's on, it's hard to keep it below freezing. Not a problem during the day, but at night it's freeze or burn. When I brought this to management's attention, they offered to switch my room but said all rooms were the same in this regard.As mentioned by others, check Expedia, they have great rates. We paid $229 the first three nights and when I checked Expedia prior to renewing, I saw a quoted rate of $185. I told the front desk this and after some haggling they extended my stay for $189. They initially told me I would have to downgrade rooms for this rate. They said I had been upgraded to the second level upon check-in. This second tier room is supposedly identical to the standard room but has a view. When I pointed out to the front desk that this room has no view without pressing your face to the window, they let us stay. This hotel is a good value. Many Boston hotel rooms (Park Plaza, The Omni) are older and not updated. I like The Charles Hotel in Cambridge - free DVD player in room, large rooms, nice views, nice area. I also like the Marriott Longwharf - large comfy rooms and the best doormen in the city, but this hotel has some great rates available.  
<Date>Aug 28, 2005
