<Author>TejasGirl
<Content>Loved Nine Zero I stayed the weekend of May 27th-30th to celebrate my boyfriend's birthday. I called to see if the hotel could place a birthday note in our room for my boyfriend upon our arrival. They not only did that, but also placed a huge delicious piece of double chocolate cake for us. My boyfriend loved it and ate the entire cake himself. The hotel was extremely clean, nice, very up to date. Bathrooms were spacious with great soaps, shampoos and a fantastic hair dryer! The mini bar was something I'd never seen before. You had your own bar with an assorment of mixers, recipe book etc. The hotel bar served good strong drinks. Sat. night we decided to rent a car for Sunday and the concierge was extremely helpful with this. We had our car ready for us by 8am Sunday morning. We drove to New Hampshire (45 min drive) and Maine ( 10 minutes from NH) to have some New England chowder and lobster rolls. This hotel is a perfect location for first timers or regulars to Boston. Hotel is directly accross from the Freedom Trail, Granary Burial Ground where John Adams, Paul Revere, John Hancock are buried. Only one thing went wrong on this wonderful trip. One of our bags was mistakenly left with hotel concierge and we had to go back to hotel to retrieve it. I'm sure this is common sense, but please remember to verify all baggage is with you before leaving your hotel. Overall, this was an awesome hotel. I highly recommend it to anyone staying in this fabulous city!

<Content>Great Hotel My wife and I stayed at the Nine Zero over the weekend of August 5th. Check-in: flawlessRoom: very niceLocation: can't beat itValue: unbelievable (paid only $125/night thru Expedia)This is a legitimate 4/5 star hotel (I've stayed at numerous Four Seasons and Ritz Carlton properties) and I couldn't believe we were able to book our room at only $125/night. In Boston, you'd probably normally pay more than that for a Holiday Inn. Would recommend it to anyone, especially business travellers or couples. Also had breakfast at the hotel restaurant and it was very good.Dinner the first night was at Hamersley's Bistro. I'd give it a 4 out of 5. Food was excellent, but service was not quite there. Dinner the second night was at Great Bay (attached to the Hotel Commonwealth). Not overly impressed with this place. No big complaints; it just didn't quite live up to the expectations that come along with a $180 bill for two people.

<Author>scooty
<Content>I love Nine Zero Nine Zero is about as close to flawless as a hotel can get. Service is professional and warm without being intrusive. The decor is sleek, modern, and cool. The view from the upper floors is fantastic, while the lower non-view rooms are cozy and a good price for Boston. Upstairs is an excellent restauarant. The location is unbeatable - right across from the Common. It's a place where you feel pampered but not fussed over. Perhaps if you want a pool or a grand lobby it isn't for you, but if you like a superb boutique hotel, this is the best. I stay here a night or two when I visit Boston, even though I could stay with relatives for free!My only complaint is the ambient techno music that plays incessantly in the lobby. Fine if you're just walking through, but if you're waiting for someone down in the lobby (as I was during a huge downpour that delayed my guests' arrival,) the music could become montonous. Well, it did for me anyway, but maybe that's just taste. I wish I had a different musical suggestion that fit the decor.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nine Zero - the best hotel I have ever stayed at Nine Zero was quite simply the best hotel experience I have ever had and I travel a lot. After my flight was delayed for over four hours, I was dying to get to the hotel and get some sleep - this hotel provided the most comfortable bed I have ever stayed in and a lot more. The concierge and bell boy were extremely helpful - immediately rushing to take my bags when I entered the hotel (I had a lot of luggage!) and the check-in process was smooth and problem free with smiles all round despite it being past midnight. The room was pretty big and there was plenty of space for all my bags, a desk with all amenities for easy work if you're on business like I was, two luxury turkish cotton robes (so nice I bought one!) and a number of removable hangers in the large wardrobe. A nice touch was the personal bar with your own margarita, cosmo, bloody mary and apple martini mixes, along with rimmers and all sizes of glasses you could possibly need with a separate well-stocked mini-bar and fresh ice bucket. The bed was a large double with feather pillows and duvet, and I literally sinked into it!The bathroom is huge, with all toiletries you could possibly need - by Mario Russo, which smelt fantastic - and a large marble shower. Only possible complaint is no bath, but I was personally more than happy with the shower. The hotel is two minutes from Boston Common and shopping centres, and five-ten mins walk from Freedom Trail locations. I also used the gym, which although reasonably small, was deserted on Sunday morning and was supplied with numerous towels, apples and water. The accompanying showers were also clean and spacious.I was more than happy to head back to my hotel and relax after the conference - the bar and restaurant is great and despite being on a busy road the hotel was very peaceful. Needless to say check-out was just as pleasant.Essentially, what more could you ask for?! Great service, great location, great amenities, great room - I'll most definitely be back.

<Content>Great Style, Comfort, Location The room was great (we needed one with two beds and it was not cramped at all! Yeah!), the staff was great, and the location is excellent! The bar was small but very chic in decor, as were all common areas and our room. Definitely NOT the stereotypical colonial Boston look, but very modern, yet always comfortable feeling. The friendly desk staff offered us umbrellas one night when it looked like rain, was always ready with restaurant suggestions and directions, and the housekeeping staff was very quick with extra mugs, coffee, towels. The city was in the middle of a record breaking heat/humid spell when we were there, but the hotel's air-conditioning was always up to the task, and easily adjustable in our room. Black-out shade at the window was welcome and mattresses were so comfortable. Have stayed at Lenox and Park Plaza and this was so much nicer. Definitely hope I get to Boston and this hotel again!  
<Date>Jun 29, 2005

<Content>Location, Location, Location!! We stayed in Nine Zero for three nights. I have to say the staff were all very friendly and helpful. The lobby area is quite small and as we like to stroll around the hotel there wasn鈥檛 much more to see there only the hotel rooms. We ventured through the bar and restaurant which also was quite small but very chic Sex in the City style. The bar and restaurant do not seem to be part of the hotel which would have been nice as the atmosphere there was electric. We also took a stroll to the fitness room which is literally three or four treadmills.. I suppose what more do you need! Needless to say we didn鈥檛 use them!! The hotel permits access to another gym, which is not directly part of the hotel. We didn鈥檛 check that out!The location couldn't be better - right at the doorstep of all the main shopping areas and two minutes walk from Fanueil Hall also known as Quincy Market. You can really soak up the atmosphere of this historic city.If its a comfortable bed you're looking for I would highly recommend this hotel, but if its atmosphere this is not the hotel for you! Enjoyed the experience but wont be back!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Overrated We stayed there for a three day weekend and found the hotel to be grossly overrated. First, we booked a suite. Big mistake. All suites are located on lower floors and have just one window that look out to an office building on Tremont Street. For nearly $650/night, we found ourselves in a dark room (the bedroom had no windows to speak of). Second, we told the hotel we were traveling with a child and repeatedly requested a crib for our baby. When we arrived, no crib. When the crib did come it was old, rickety and not all that safe. Moreover, there was no room for the crib in the bedroom and the hotel concierge suggested that we push it up against the wall facing the open electrical outlets. We understand that not all hotels are outfitted to cater to children, but having made the explicit request well in advance, we had expected at least our room to be child friendly. Third, our room was in a state of disrepair. Food stains on the couch, lampshades that had burn marks from where the lightbulb had burned through, hair in the bathtub, and enough grit on the carpet that it wasn't pleasant walking barefoot through the room. Even the hotel acknowledged that our $650/night room was sub-par. Fourth, the service was not in keeping with its rating at all. We complained to the hotel manager who never showed his face. We got one voicemail message and that was it. Never heard from him again. After repeated complaints to the front desk, they knocked off $100/night on our room which didn't seem like adequate consolation, but we were just so glad to be out of the hotel we did not care at that point. We are not picky travelers who require every pillow to be fluffed and duvets to be just so. We just require value for the money we are spending. I am pretty sure that had we stayed at the Four Seasons or Ritz Carlton, the service and amenities would have been worth the money we paid. As it was, we felt like we were being robbed every night that we stayed at Nine Zero. I would definitely not recommend. At this price point, there are better options.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Comparison Nine Zero and Onyx Stayed in March and April of 05 for a few days in the Onyx and at the Nine Zero. Yes, both of them are so called boutique hotels and there are some differences but as usual it all depends how you weight them. Overall I had a pleasant experience in both hotels but would both not consider as 4 star hotels. I stayed in the lowest room category at both hotels and both had fairly small rooms and bathrooms. If I go again with my company I would probably choose the Nine Zero.Onyx:Plus: - Location fairly central- Up to $70 cheaper per night then the Nine Zero (sometimes good internet deals)- You can keep the CD they have at the room- Free internetNegative:- Low key bar (it not a restaurant)- Staff sometimes a bit slow with taxi ordering- - No gym (pass is offered to close by sports club but club is not up to standard)Nine ZeroPlus:- Very central location- Excellent restaurant- Free internetNegative- Can be much more expensive then Onyx- Mini gym (pass is offered to close by sports club but club is not up to standard)

<Author>Tampa_Law_Guy
<Content>Think a W without the attitude Just spent three nights at Nine Zero with my partner and was glad to see that it lived up to the hype. Check-in was smooth. We had originally booked an intimate room through Quikbook and upgraded to a fantastic room for $25 more a night. The employees at the front desk were always helpful. The lobby is fairly small. There is a living room-like space to the immediate right once you enter the lobby. It has some comfortable sofas and chairs to relax in while waiting to go out or even to read the paper in the morning. The decor is very modern and streamlined, but with good use of warm colors to make it feel more inviting. The room was a good size with a king bed that was very comfortable. The duvet is very warm and comfy as well. The room is decorated in earth tones and the furniture is very modern, black, but very functional. The one thing we did laugh at was that it seemed like everything in the room had a price tag. There is a price list in the entertainment center that gives you the price for snacks and drinks, but also t-shirts, stuffed bear, playing cards, baseball caps and even a condom set all bearing the Nine Zero name and logo! You can even buy the Mario Russo products in the bathroom from them!The bathroom was a good size, decorated in white and gray marble. The aforementioned Mario Russo products were very nice. I would have loved a double vanity, but the space did not seem to be an issue with just one sink. The fitness center is pretty basic but all you would need at a hotel. The business center on the third floor was convenient as I needed to send and receive faxes during the trip. The hotel provides complimentary high speed interest access in all rooms, which was very nice, except that I got 5 viruses over the weekend that I needed to have removed from my laptop. Our only complaint was that the room did get a bit warm at night in spite of turning the air control all the way to the cool setting. While it may have been 30 degrees outside, the room was a bit stuffy overnight because they pumped in heated air regardless of your individual control settings.As far as the location, the hotel is in a pretty quiet area at night. During week days, it is a bit more animated as the business district is to the back of the hotel. The hotel is about two blocks from the Government Center T stop and about two blocks in the other direction from the Park Street T stop at Boston Common. This makes it very easy to get around the city on the various subway lines. While we took a taxi cab in the night we got in, we walked over to the Government Center T stop the last day and caught the subway to the Airport stop. It cost only $1.25 a person and took only 15 minutes. You then board a bus from the station that takes you directly to your departing terminal. All in all, I would say that the Nine Zero was a pleasant experience and that we enjoyed the facilities and customer service. We would definitely consider staying there again on a return trip to Boston.

<Content>My new favorite hotel in Boston Just got back from celebrating my one year wedding anniversary at the Nine Zero in Boston. Before we even got there, we were pleased with the wonderful service. We were suppose to be there the weekend of the blizzard (Jan 22), but had to cancel obviously. They cancelled our reservation the morning we were suppose to check in no questions asked then rebooked us on Valentine's weekend for the same rate even though the rate should have been $60 higher. Upon arrival, we were treated with first class service from the bellman/valet to the front desk attendant. Check-in took less than five minutes and when we go to the room, someone had gone in right before we arrived and turned on the stereo for some music upon entry. The room was excellent, appointed very nicely. The martini set was a nice little touch, different from your normal hotel. The only complaint with the room was it was too hot. But being an old building, they can only have hot air or cool air coming out of the vents, so we just turned it off and opened the windor a bit. The location was great, right on the Freedom trail, short walk to the common. We actually walked back from Copley Square, which in the winter was a bit rough, but in the summer would be a nice little stroll. I would definitely recommend this hotel if your staying in Boston for someplace to stay that is not like your typical Marriott, Hyat, Westin, etc. Similar to a W Hotel, only nice in my opinion.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Simply Amazing! I stayed at Nine Zero for two nights (Nov 21-22, 2004) and had an amazing experience. When I first checked into my Fantastic room, it had a queen bed and seemed a bit small, but had a window overlooking Boston Common. I immediately called the front desk, who offered to move me to a larger room on the other side of the building that had no view. Since I didn't intend to be in my hotel room much during the visit, I thought this was a worthy trade -- and, in retrospect, I made the right decision! My bigger Fantastic room had a king bed and was very spacious. The amenties in the bathroom were terriffic and the overall decor was very chic. The staff was extremely courteous and helpful. Perhaps the best part was the location- right off of Boston Common, you can walk almost anywhere in a hurry (plus, the T station is a block away on the direct line to Harvard).One downside was that the hotel lobby is rather small and uninviting. While it's fashionably decorated, the lobby makes for a poor waiting room. My only other issue was the price of room service: $40 for soup/sandwich/juice seemed excessive.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Tops in the Hub! Stayed here three nights in November 2004 in a spectacular room, and it was! The view of Beacon Hill, the Boston Common, the State House, etc. was awesome. The staff is very friendly and definitely interested in making their guests comfortable and happy. The decor is ultra modern. The room was very clean. The toiletries are great quality. The bed was simply one of the most comfortable I've ever had the pleasure of using. They offer 'turn-down' service in the evening and they replace towels (if they've been used), fill the ice bucket, etc. It's all very nice. The location is wonderful: easy walking distance to many sites and a stone's throw to the public transportation system if you do not want to walk. Oh! They also provide you with umbrellas to use during your stay if needed.One small complaint: the water pressure in the shower was poor. However, since everthing else was truly wonderful, it was only a small nuisance. I'd come back in a heartbeat!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Modern but still cosy We stayed at Nine Zero for 3 nights at the beginning of September. When booking I had advised we would be on our honeymoon and that we would appreciate a room with a good view of the city. We had booked a 'fantastic' room - and we got a fantastic view - definitely worth asking for! The hotel also surprised us with champagne and strawberries. The room was clean, of an average size  the decor was sleek and modern but still cosy. The bed was very comfortable and the toiletries provided in the bathroom smelt so nice I took them with me! We found every member of staff to be proactive, friendly, very efficient and helpful - and to remember who we were. The hotel is very well located for seeing the city and the sights although the downside of this was that we found the city noise to be a bit much at night. The only other downside was that the room had only a shower and no bath which I would have expected for a hotel in this price range. We loved Boston and intend to visit again. We would certainly consider the Nine Zero - and if they would only soundproof those windows we would return without a doubt....Also - loved the 'cocktail' minibar - every hotel should have one like that!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Hotel blunted only by Spire Have just returned from an amazing holiday in America, four nights of which were spent at Nine Zero. Whilst you cannot, no doubt, please everyone previous reviews criticising the staff and service seem entirely unjustified. The most helpful bell trolley and reception service greeted us whenever we needed it. The feel of the hotel was trendy but relaxed. The rooms we had were to a very high standard. Our last night stopover (after a 4 night trip to Cape Cod) included a free upgraded room (which was a genuine upgrade from the room we had first stayed in - which we had been more than happy with).The one slight disappointment - our meal in Spire. It just tried too hard with overly fussy food and seems to have been over-hyped by the available reviews. There are plenty other great places to eat in Boston - but for accomodation I cant see it being beaten. When I return to Boston I will stay here again

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>beautiful, hip in a great location My husband and I stayed at Nine Zero from Aug 13-16, 2004. I was a bit nervous reading the bad reviews, but we had no problems with the hotel. We had the smallest room, which really was quite small, but it was very well appointed and laid out. The free high speed internet was great. The bed is very comfy with plenty of pillows. The hotel design is very contemporary which we enjoy. We enjoyed having cocktails at the spire bar ( I especially enjoyed the flirtini). We had breakfast on Sat morning at Spire and while it was good-it was very expensive (I did notice that they have a separate breakfast menu for the weekdays and the prices are lower). The service was great and all staff members were very friendly and helpful (they even kept my cannoli chilled in their refrigerator for me overnight!) The hotel is very conviently located near Boston Common. It's a short walk to Fanueil Hall, the North End and Newberry Street. We would definitely return to this hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>All style, no substance We booked this hotel because it looked stylish. The location is suberb, as are the rooms. Comfy beds, a spacious shower and fab toiletries.There the luxury ends. Not only was the champagne not waiting, but when I enquired at reception as to where it was, I was asked if I had booked it at the right hotel. I phoned and complained and was assured, after faxing them a copy of my bill, that they would get back to me. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice Hotel, Poor Service I stayed at the hotel for several weeks on business and found it to be uneven at best.The hotel itself is nice. The design is modern and chic, but inviting. The rooms have some nice amenities, including comfortable beds and a fast internet connection.The young-ish staff, on the other hand, seemed inexperienced and unschooled in hospitality. Wake-up calls and breakfast frequently arrived late, if at all. A colleague's laundry was lost for several days. Maids began knocking on doors at 8 a.m.By far the worst experience of my stay, however, was being bumped from my room. I awoke one morning to find my bill placed under the door. When I called to inquire why, I was told that my reservation had ended and that the hotel was fully booked for the evening. Incredulous, I asked the hotel's reservations desk to look into this and fix what must have been a simple mistake on their part. I was greeted, alternately, with indifference, denials and blame. Worst of all, the staff made no attempt to rectify their error in any way, even by offering to find me a room at another hotel. Over time, the hotel may iron out its service problems, but for now I would not recommend it.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great location, Great value, Great service Nine Zero has the basic look and feel of an Ian Shrager hotel (Royalton, Paramount, Mercer -- cool ambiance, fashionable, minimalist), but MUCH bigger rooms and MUCH less expensive. The staff is very friendly and accomodating, and the food is definitely better than most hotel cuisine at similar price levels. It's located right downtown -- meaning a very short walk to Downtown Crossing, the Financial District (Post Office Square), Fanueil Hall, and Boston Commons. It's also about a 7 minute cab ride to Copley/Prudential and Newbury Street shopping. They also have a great in-house car service that is the same price as a cab, but the difference being that it is a brand new minivan with an 18 LCD playing DVDs to watch while you're being whisked around Boston by a very friendly driver employed by Nine Zero. Really enjoyed our stay, and definitely recommend it.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A true pleasure I stayed at the Nine Zero for a recent weekend in Boston, and am pleased to report that it is one of the few hotels I've EVER stayed at which I felt was worth its cost. The room (smallest version, Intimate) was not huge, but was fantastically comfortable, very stylish, and impeccably cleaned and prepared (with the trivial exception of a missing bulb in the desk lamp-- which was immediately remedied by the staff, along with an extra bathrobe I requested.) My room on the 14th floor was not supposed to have any view at all, but actually looked out directly at the Old North Church. I had brought a bottle of wine from home, with a corkscrew-- but was pleased to find a corkscrew and wine glasses already in the room. Check in and check out were civilized and efficient. Staff in the hallways were cheerful and polite. The location is unbeatable. I grew up in Boston, and have rarely stayed in hotels in my home city-- but the experience at Nine Zero was so delightful I expect to make a habit of it.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>fabulous hotel for business travel I stayed at Nine Zero while in town for business. My only regret was that I could only stay one night! Everything was wonderful, from the bell person who not only dug my luggage out of the taxi, but set up my (complimentary!) high-speed internet access before leaving my room, to the comfortable bed, to the great shower. The rooms are not the standard cookie-cutter decor, and I appreciated the change. Also, I have to mention the room service. I'm usually wary about room service, but tried it here, and was pleasantly surprised. I had a delicious meal - home made pasta with wild mushrooms, fresh asparagus, and perfectly grilled chicken - at a reasonable price. I really can't imagine staying anywhere else when in Boston for business.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fabulous I went to the Nine Zero for my birthday. I loved the place. The rooms are so modern that they're retro...or vice versa. However you look at it, they did a good job selecting fixtures, linens, architects, location, anything you can mention.I loved that the chair was ergonomic. I loved that the TV and entertainment center was recessed into the wall, so that even a small room felt bigger. I loved that the mattress was comfier than mine at home. And, I loved that I could go anywhere in Boston so easily from the hotel...mostly walking, but also within a block of 2 or 3 T stations.If you like a hotel staff to smile and use your name and all that, you'll love it.My only hesitation in calling this place the best available is that I was there during a slow week...so I don't know how they handle a full house. Even then, I can't imagine a night or two at the Nine Zero to be anything less than fabulous.

<Author>Vermontman
<Content>My new Boston home Booked Nine Zero in August, 2003 for an overnight business trip. As Boston is a regular business destination for me, I am usually unhappy about the price to value ratio as Boston has too few hotels which charge far too much for what you get. I found Nine Zero on the web on short notice and hoped that the hotel looked something like the website. What a pleasant surprise. The rooms are fun-- the decorator must have been given free rein. The restuarant was excellent, the bar convivial, and the location perfect---Samuel Adams is buried in the Common right across the street. I spent ten minutes looking at the decor in the restaurant close up-- from the lampshades to the curtains, and marvelled at the taste and creativity. Good staff--all very cheerful, and well priced. My one night business trip was like a short vacation thanks to Nine Zero.

<Author>MableUpstateny
<Content>not totally up to their image Stayed there in July, 2003. The first room we were checked into had very damp carpeting--from being recently cleaned. Not pleasant in bare or stockinged feet. They moved us (to a room with a less pleasant view), and that room needed a good dusting--baseboards, furniture trim, blinds. Cleanliness of rooms is important in any hotel, but particularly in these boutique hotels that are so much about image and design details. Dust doesn't compliment the effort to be both modern and comfortable. Other than that, the rooms are nicely appointed--good beds and linens, chairs, etc.The bar was okay--but we preferred the bar at the Parker House down the street. We had dinner at the Spire, their restaurant which was also fine--but I wouldn't say fantastic.The staff were pleasant--and the concierge helpful.Location is good--although somewhat difficult to find if you're driving. Once you're there you can walk or take the subway easily.
